South Africa signed the Rio [Convention on Biological Diversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity "Convention on Biological Diversity") on 4 June 1994 and became a party to the convention on 2 November 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-137"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> It has subsequently produced a [National Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity_action_plan "Biodiversity action plan"), which was received by the convention on 7 June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-cbd.int_138-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-cbd.int-138">[138]</a></sup> The country is ranked sixth out of the world's seventeen [megadiverse countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megadiverse_countries "Megadiverse countries").<sup id="cite_ref-139"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> [Ecotourism in South Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecotourism_in_South_Africa "Ecotourism in South Africa") has become more prevalent in recent years, as a possible method of maintaining and improving biodiversity.

Numerous mammals are found in the Bushveld including lions, [African leopards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_leopard "African leopard"), [South African cheetahs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_African_cheetah "Southeast African cheetah"), [southern white rhinos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_white_rhinoceros "Southern white rhinoceros"), [blue wildebeest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_wildebeest "Blue wildebeest"), [kudus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kudu "Kudu"), [impalas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impala "Impala"), [hyenas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyena "Hyena"), [hippopotamuses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippopotamus "Hippopotamus") and [South African giraffes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_giraffe "South African giraffe"). A significant extent of the Bushveld exists in the north-east including Kruger National Park and the [Sabi Sand Game Reserve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabi_Sand_Game_Reserve "Sabi Sand Game Reserve"), as well as in the far north in the [Waterberg Biosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterberg_Biosphere "Waterberg Biosphere"). South Africa houses many [endemic species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endemism "Endemism"), among them the critically endangered [riverine rabbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riverine_rabbit "Riverine rabbit") (_Bunolagus monticullaris_) in the Karoo.

Up to 1945, more than 4,900 species of [fungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungus "Fungus") (including [lichen-forming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lichen#Fungi "Lichen") species) had been recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-140"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In 2006, the number of fungi in South Africa was estimated at 200,000 species but did not take into account fungi associated with insects.<sup id="cite_ref-141"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> If correct, then the number of South African fungi dwarfs that of its plants. In at least some major South African ecosystems, an exceptionally high percentage of fungi are highly specific in terms of the plants with which they occur.<sup id="cite_ref-142"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> The country's Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan does not mention fungi (including lichen-forming fungi).<sup id="cite_ref-cbd.int_138-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-cbd.int-138">[138]</a></sup>

With more than 22,000 different [vascular plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vascular_plant "Vascular plant"), or about 9% of all the known species of plants on Earth,<sup id="cite_ref-143"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> South Africa is particularly rich in plant diversity. The most prevalent biome is the [grassland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grassland "Grassland"), particularly on the Highveld, where the plant cover is dominated by different [grasses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poaceae "Poaceae"), low shrubs, and [acacia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acacia "Acacia"), mainly camel-thorn (_[Vachellia erioloba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vachellia_erioloba "Vachellia erioloba")_). Vegetation is sparse towards the north-west because of low rainfall. There are numerous species of water-storing succulents, like [aloes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aloe "Aloe") and [euphorbias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euphorbia "Euphorbia"), in the very hot and dry Namaqualand area. And according to the [World Wildlife Fund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature "World Wide Fund for Nature"), South Africa is home to around a third of all succulent species.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_144-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-:1-144">[144]</a></sup> The grass and thorn [savanna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Savanna "Savanna") turns slowly into a bush savanna towards the north-east of the country, with denser growth. There are significant numbers of [baobab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adansonia "Adansonia") trees in this area, near the northern end of Kruger National Park.<sup id="cite_ref-145"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>

The fynbos biome, which makes up the majority of the area and plant life in the [Cape Floristic Region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Floristic_Region "Cape Floristic Region"), is located in a small region of the Western Cape and contains more than 9,000 of those species, or three times more plant species than found in the [Amazon rainforest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_rainforest "Amazon rainforest"),<sup id="cite_ref-146"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> making it among the richest regions on earth in terms of plant diversity. Most of the plants are [evergreen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evergreen "Evergreen") hard-leaf plants with fine, needle-like leaves, such as the [sclerophyllous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sclerophyll "Sclerophyll") plants. Another uniquely South African flowering plant group is the genus _[Protea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protea "Protea")_, with around 130 different species. While South Africa has a great wealth of flowering plants, only 1% of the land is forest, almost exclusively in the humid [coastal plain of KwaZulu-Natal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KwaZulu%E2%80%93Cape_coastal_forest_mosaic "KwaZulu–Cape coastal forest mosaic"), where there are also areas of [Southern Africa mangroves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Africa_mangroves "Southern Africa mangroves") in river mouths. Even smaller reserves of forests are out of the reach of fire, known as [montane forests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knysna%E2%80%93Amatole_montane_forests "Knysna–Amatole montane forests"). Plantations of imported tree species are predominant, particularly the non-native [eucalyptus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eucalyptus "Eucalyptus") and pine.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flora_at_Cape_Peninsula.JPG/220px-Flora_at_Cape_Peninsula.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Flora_at_Cape_Peninsula.JPG)

[Cape Floral Region Protected Areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas "Cape Floral Region Protected Areas")

South Africa has lost a large area of natural habitat in the last four decades, primarily because of overpopulation, sprawling development patterns, and deforestation during the 19th century. The country had a 2019 [Forest Landscape Integrity Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index "Forest Landscape Integrity Index") mean score of 4.94/10, ranking it 112th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_147-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-147">[147]</a></sup> South Africa is one of the worst affected countries in the world when it comes to invasion by [alien species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Introduced_species "Introduced species") with many (e.g., [black wattle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acacia_mearnsii "Acacia mearnsii"), [Port Jackson willow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acacia_saligna "Acacia saligna"), _[Hakea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hakea "Hakea")_, _[Lantana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lantana "Lantana")_ and _[Jacaranda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacaranda "Jacaranda")_) posing a significant threat to the native biodiversity and the already scarce water resources. Also [woody plant encroachment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woody_plant_encroachment "Woody plant encroachment") of native plants in grasslands poses a threat to biodiversity and related ecosystem services, affecting over 7 million hectares.<sup id="cite_ref-148"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The original [temperate forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forests "Temperate broadleaf and mixed forests") found by the first European settlers was exploited until only small patches remained. Currently, South African hardwood trees like [real yellowwood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_yellowwood "Real yellowwood") (_[Podocarpus latifolius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Podocarpus_latifolius "Podocarpus latifolius")_), stinkwood (_[Ocotea bullata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocotea_bullata "Ocotea bullata")_), and South African black ironwood (_[Olea capensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olea_capensis "Olea capensis")_) are under strict government protection. Statistics from the [Department of Environmental Affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_of_Environment,_Forestry_and_Fisheries "Department of Environment, Forestry and Fisheries") show a record 1,215 rhinos were killed in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-149"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Since South Africa is home to a third of all succulent species (many endemic to the Karoo), it makes it a hotspot for plant poaching, leading to many species to be threatened with extinction.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_144-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-:1-144">[144]</a></sup>

## Demographics

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg/220px-South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_(hex_cells).svg)

Map of population density in South Africa

-     <1 /km<sup>2</sup>
    
-     1–3 /km<sup>2</sup>
    
-     3–10 /km<sup>2</sup>
    
-     10–30 /km<sup>2</sup>
    
-     30–100 /km<sup>2</sup>
    
-     100–300 /km<sup>2</sup>
    
-     300–1000 /km<sup>2</sup>
    
-     1000–3000 /km<sup>2</sup>
    
-     >3000 /km<sup>2</sup>
    

South Africa is a nation of about 62 million (as of 2022) people of diverse origins, cultures, languages, and religions.<sup id="cite_ref-150"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The last [census](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_National_Census_of_2022 "South African National Census of 2022") was held in 2022, with estimates produced on an annual basis. According to the United Nations' _[World Population Prospects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Population_Prospects "World Population Prospects")_, South Africa's total population was 55.3 million in 2015, compared to only 13.6 million in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-151"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> South Africa is home to an estimated five million [illegal immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illegal_immigration "Illegal immigration"), including some three million Zimbabweans.<sup id="cite_ref-152"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> A series of [anti-immigrant riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xenophobia_in_South_Africa "Xenophobia in South Africa") occurred beginning in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_155-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-bbc-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup>

[Statistics South Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics_South_Africa "Statistics South Africa") asks people to describe themselves in the census in terms of five racial population groups.<sup id="cite_ref-157"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> The 2022 census figures for these groups were: [Black African](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bantu_peoples_of_South_Africa "Bantu peoples of South Africa") at 81%, [Coloured](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Coloureds "Cape Coloureds") at 8.2%, [White](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_South_Africans "White South Africans") at 7.3%, [Indian or Asian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_South_Africans "Indian South Africans") at 2.7%, and Other/Unspecified at 0.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_158-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-auto1-158">[158]</a></sup> The first census in 1911 showed that whites made up 22% of the population; this had declined to 16% by 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-159"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>

South Africa hosts a sizeable refugee and asylum seeker population. According to the _World Refugee Survey 2008_, published by the [U.S. Committee for Refugees and Immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Committee_for_Refugees_and_Immigrants "U.S. Committee for Refugees and Immigrants"), this population numbered approximately 144,700 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_160-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-160">[160]</a></sup> Groups of refugees and asylum seekers numbering over 10,000 included people from Zimbabwe (48,400), the DRC (24,800), and Somalia (12,900).<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_160-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-160">[160]</a></sup> These populations mainly lived in Johannesburg, Pretoria, [Durban](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durban "Durban"), Cape Town, and [Port Elizabeth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_Elizabeth "Port Elizabeth").<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_160-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-160">[160]</a></sup>

### Languages

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg/220px-South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:South_Africa_2011_dominant_language_map_(hex_cells).svg)

South Africa has 12 official languages:<sup id="cite_ref-parliament.gov.za_4-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-parliament.gov.za-4">[4]</a></sup> [Zulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zulu_language "Zulu language"), [Xhosa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xhosa_language "Xhosa language"), [Afrikaans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afrikaans "Afrikaans"), [English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_English "South African English"), [Pedi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Sotho "Northern Sotho"),<sup id="cite_ref-161"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> [Tswana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tswana_language "Tswana language"), [Southern Sotho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sotho_language "Sotho language"), [Tsonga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsonga_language "Tsonga language"), [Swazi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swazi_language "Swazi language"), [Venda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venda_language "Venda language"), and [Southern Ndebele](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Ndebele_language "Southern Ndebele language") (in order of first language speakers), as well as South African Sign Language which was recognised as an official language in 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-parliament.gov.za_4-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-parliament.gov.za-4">[4]</a></sup>In this regard it is fourth only to [Bolivia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolivia "Bolivia"), [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_languages_of_India "Official languages of India"), and [Zimbabwe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zimbabwe "Zimbabwe") in number. While all the languages are formally equal, some languages are spoken more than others. According to the 2022 census, the three most spoken first languages are Zulu (24.4%), Xhosa (16.6%), and Afrikaans (10.6%).<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_158-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-auto1-158">[158]</a></sup> Although English is recognised as the language of commerce and science, it is only the fifth most common home language, that of only 8.7% of South Africans in 2022; nevertheless, it has become the de facto [lingua franca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lingua_franca "Lingua franca") of the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_158-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-auto1-158">[158]</a></sup> Estimates based on the 1991 census suggest just under half of South Africans could speak English.<sup id="cite_ref-162"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> It is the second most commonly spoken language outside of the household, after Zulu.<sup id="cite_ref-163"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>

Other languages are spoken, or were widely used previously, including [Fanagalo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fanagalo_language "Fanagalo language"), [Khoe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khoe_language "Khoe language"), [Lobedu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lobedu_language "Lobedu language"), [Nama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nama_language "Nama language"), [Northern Ndebele](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Ndebele_language "Northern Ndebele language"), and [Phuthi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phuthi_language "Phuthi language").<sup id="cite_ref-164"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Many of the unofficial [languages of the San and Khoekhoe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khoisan_languages "Khoisan languages") peoples contain regional dialects stretching northwards into Namibia and Botswana, and elsewhere. These people, who are a physically distinct population from the Bantu people who make up most of the Black Africans in South Africa, have their own cultural identity based on their [hunter-gatherer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter-gatherer "Hunter-gatherer") societies. They have been marginalised, and the remainder of their languages are in danger of becoming [extinct](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinct_language "Extinct language").

White South Africans may also speak European languages, including Italian, Portuguese (also spoken by black Angolans and Mozambicans), Dutch, German, and Greek, while some Indian South Africans and more recent migrants from South Asia speak [Indian languages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Languages_of_India "Languages of India"), such as Gujarati, Hindi, Tamil, Telugu, and Urdu. French is spoken by migrants from [Francophone Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_French "African French").

### Religion

According to the 2001 census, Christians accounted for 79.8% of the population, with a majority of them being members of various [Protestant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestantism "Protestantism") [denominations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_denomination "Christian denomination") (broadly defined to include [syncretic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syncretism "Syncretism") [African-initiated churches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African-initiated_church "African-initiated church")) and a minority of [Roman Catholics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church") and other Christians. Christian category includes [Zion Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zion_Christian_Church "Zion Christian Church") (11.1%), [Pentecostal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pentecostalism "Pentecostalism") ([Charismatic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charismatic_movement "Charismatic movement")) (8.2%), [Roman Catholic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_South_Africa "Catholic Church in South Africa") (7.1%), [Methodist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Southern_Africa "Methodist Church of Southern Africa") (6.8%), [Dutch Reformed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church_in_South_Africa_(NGK) "Dutch Reformed Church in South Africa (NGK)") (6.7%), and [Anglican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Southern_Africa "Anglican Church of Southern Africa") (3.8%). Members of remaining Christian churches accounted for another 36% of the population. [Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_South_Africa "Islam in South Africa") accounted for 1.5% of the population, [Hindus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism_in_South_Africa "Hinduism in South Africa") 1.2%,<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_166-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-state.gov-166">[166]</a></sup> [traditional African religions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_African_religions "Traditional African religions") 0.3% and Judaism 0.2%. 15.1% had no religious affiliation, 0.6% were "other" and 1.4% were "unspecified."<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_167-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-factbook-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_166-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-state.gov-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup>

African-initiated churches formed the largest of the Christian groups. It was believed that many of the persons who claimed no affiliation with any organised religion adhered to a traditional African religion. There are an estimated 200,000 [traditional healers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_healers_of_Southern_Africa "Traditional healers of Southern Africa"), and up to 60% of South Africans consult these healers,<sup id="cite_ref-170"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> generally called _sangoma_ ('diviner') or _inyanga_ ('herbalist'). These healers use a combination of [ancestral spiritual beliefs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veneration_of_the_dead "Veneration of the dead") and a belief in the spiritual and medicinal properties of local fauna, flora, and funga commonly known as [_muti_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_African_medicine "Traditional African medicine") ('medicine'), to facilitate healing in clients. Many peoples have syncretic religious practices combining Christian and indigenous influences.<sup id="cite_ref-DoS_171-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-DoS-171">[171]</a></sup>

South African Muslims comprise mainly Coloureds and Indians. They have been joined by black or white South African converts as well as those from other parts of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-csmonitor_172-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-csmonitor-172">[172]</a></sup> South African Muslims describe their faith as the fastest-growing religion of conversion in the country, with the number of black Muslims growing sixfold, from 12,000 in 1991 to 74,700 in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-csmonitor_172-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-csmonitor-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>

There is a substantial [Jewish population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_South_Africa "History of the Jews in South Africa"), descended from [European Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Europe "History of the Jews in Europe") who arrived as a minority among other European settlers. This population peaked in the 1970s at 118,000, though only around 75,000 remain today, the rest having emigrated, mostly to Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-174"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Even so, these numbers make the Jewish community in South Africa the twelfth largest in the world.

### Education

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/UCT_Upper_Campus_landscape_view.jpg/220px-UCT_Upper_Campus_landscape_view.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:UCT_Upper_Campus_landscape_view.jpg)

The [University of Cape Town](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Cape_Town "University of Cape Town")

The adult [literacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literacy "Literacy") rate in 2007 was 89%.<sup id="cite_ref-unescolit_175-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-unescolit-175">[175]</a></sup> South Africa has a [three-tier system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three-tier_education "Three-tier education") of education starting with primary school, followed by high school, and tertiary education in the form of (academic) universities and universities of technology. Learners have twelve years of formal schooling, from grade 1 to 12. Grade R, or grade 0, is a pre-primary foundation year.<sup id="cite_ref-edufacts0831_176-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-edufacts0831-176">[176]</a></sup> Primary schools span the first seven years of schooling.<sup id="cite_ref-177"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> High school education spans a further five years. The [National Senior Certificate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matriculation_in_South_Africa "Matriculation in South Africa") examination takes place at the end of grade 12 and is necessary for tertiary studies at a [South African university](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_universities_in_South_Africa "List of universities in South Africa").<sup id="cite_ref-edufacts0831_176-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-edufacts0831-176">[176]</a></sup> Public universities are divided into three types: traditional universities, which offer theoretically oriented university degrees; [universities of technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_of_technology "Institute of technology") (formerly called _[technikons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technikon "Technikon")_), which offer vocationally-oriented diplomas and degrees; and comprehensive universities, which offer both types of qualification. There are 23 public universities in South Africa: 11 traditional universities, 6 universities of technology, and 6 comprehensive universities.

Under apartheid, schools for black people were subject to discrimination through inadequate funding and a separate syllabus called _[Bantu Education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bantu_Education_Act,_1953 "Bantu Education Act, 1953")_ which only taught skills sufficient to work as labourers.<sup id="cite_ref-178"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup>

In 2004, South Africa started reforming its tertiary education system, merging and incorporating small universities into larger institutions, and renaming all tertiary education institutions "university". By 2015, 1.4 million students in higher education have been aided by a financial aid scheme which was promulgated in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-Cele_179-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-Cele-179">[179]</a></sup>

### Health

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Tygerberg_from_air.jpg/220px-Tygerberg_from_air.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tygerberg_from_air.jpg)

[Tygerberg Hospital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tygerberg_Hospital "Tygerberg Hospital") in [Parow, Cape Town](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parow,_South_Africa "Parow, South Africa")

According to the [South African Institute of Race Relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Institute_of_Race_Relations "South African Institute of Race Relations"), the life expectancy in 2009 was 71 years for a white South African and 48 years for a black South African.<sup id="cite_ref-180"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> The healthcare spending in the country is about 9% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-smartpl_181-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-smartpl-181">[181]</a></sup> About 84% of the population depends on the public healthcare system,<sup id="cite_ref-smartpl_181-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-smartpl-181">[181]</a></sup> which is beset with chronic human resource shortages and limited resources.<sup id="cite_ref-icap_182-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-icap-182">[182]</a></sup> About 20% of the population use private healthcare.<sup id="cite_ref-fmhealth_183-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-fmhealth-183">[183]</a></sup> Only 16% of the population are covered by [medical aid schemes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_insurance "Health insurance");<sup id="cite_ref-medicl_184-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-medicl-184">[184]</a></sup> the rest pay for private care [out-of-pocket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Out-of-pocket_expense "Out-of-pocket expense") or through in-hospital-only plans.<sup id="cite_ref-fmhealth_183-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-fmhealth-183">[183]</a></sup> The three dominant hospital groups, [Mediclinic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediclinic_International "Mediclinic International"), [Life Healthcare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LIFE_Healthcare_Group "LIFE Healthcare Group") and [Netcare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netcare "Netcare"), together control 75% of the private hospital market.<sup id="cite_ref-fmhealth_183-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-fmhealth-183">[183]</a></sup>

#### HIV/AIDS

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Life_expectancy_in_select_African_countries%2C_1950%E2%80%932019.jpg/220px-Life_expectancy_in_select_African_countries%2C_1950%E2%80%932019.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_select_African_countries,_1950%E2%80%932019.jpg)

Life expectancy in select Southern African countries, 1950–2019. [HIV/AIDS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HIV/AIDS "HIV/AIDS") has caused a fall in life expectancy.

According to the 2015 [UNAIDS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_United_Nations_Programme_on_HIV/AIDS "Joint United Nations Programme on HIV/AIDS") medical report, South Africa has an estimated seven million people who are living with HIV – more than any other country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-185"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> In 2018, HIV prevalence—the percentage of people living with HIV—among adults (15–49 years) was 20.4%, and in the same year 71,000 people died from an AIDS-related illness.<sup id="cite_ref-186"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>

A 2008 study revealed that HIV/AIDS infection is distinctly divided along racial lines: 13.6% of blacks are HIV-positive, whereas only 0.3% of whites have the virus.<sup id="cite_ref-ten_187-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-ten-187">[187]</a></sup> Most deaths are experienced by economically active individuals, resulting in many [AIDS orphans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AIDS_orphan "AIDS orphan") who in many cases depend on the state for care and financial support.<sup id="cite_ref-avertaids_188-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-avertaids-188">[188]</a></sup> It is estimated that there are 1,200,000 orphans in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-avertaids_188-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-avertaids-188">[188]</a></sup>

The link between HIV, a virus spread primarily by sexual contact, and AIDS was long [denied](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HIV/AIDS_denialism "HIV/AIDS denialism") by President [Thabo Mbeki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thabo_Mbeki "Thabo Mbeki") and his health minister [Manto Tshabalala-Msimang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manto_Tshabalala-Msimang "Manto Tshabalala-Msimang"), who insisted that the many deaths in the country are caused by [malnutrition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malnutrition_in_South_Africa "Malnutrition in South Africa"), and hence poverty, and not HIV.<sup id="cite_ref-189"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> In 2007, in response to international pressure, the government made efforts to fight AIDS.<sup id="cite_ref-www.info.gov.za_190-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-www.info.gov.za-190">[190]</a></sup> After the [2009 general elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_South_African_general_election "2009 South African general election"), President Jacob Zuma appointed [Aaron Motsoaledi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aaron_Motsoaledi "Aaron Motsoaledi") as the health minister and committed his government to increasing funding for and widening the scope of HIV treatment,<sup id="cite_ref-191"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> and by 2015, South Africa had made significant progress, with the widespread availability of [antiretroviral drugs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Management_of_HIV/AIDS "Management of HIV/AIDS") resulted in an increase in life expectancy from 52.1 years to 62.5 years.<sup id="cite_ref-conversationHIVExcelled_192-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-conversationHIVExcelled-192">[192]</a></sup>

## Government and Politics

[![Photo of the Union Buildings](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Uniegebou.jpg/220px-Uniegebou.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Uniegebou.jpg)

[Union Buildings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_Buildings "Union Buildings") in Pretoria, seat of the executive

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Cape_Town%2C_Houses_of_Parliament.JPG/220px-Cape_Town%2C_Houses_of_Parliament.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cape_Town,_Houses_of_Parliament.JPG)

Houses of [Parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Africa "Parliament of South Africa") in Cape Town, seat of the legislature

[![Photo of the Constitutional Court](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa.jpg/220px-Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa.jpg)

[Constitutional Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa "Constitutional Court of South Africa") in Johannesburg

South Africa is a [parliamentary republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_republic "Parliamentary republic"), but unlike most such republics, the [president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_South_Africa "President of South Africa") is both [head of state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_state "Head of state") and [head of government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_government "Head of government") and depends for their tenure on the [confidence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confidence_and_supply "Confidence and supply") of [Parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Africa "Parliament of South Africa"). The executive, legislature, and judiciary are all subject to the supremacy of the [Constitution of South Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa "Constitution of South Africa"), and the [superior courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Courts_of_South_Africa "Courts of South Africa") have the power to strike down executive actions and acts of Parliament if they are unconstitutional. The [National Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Assembly_of_South_Africa "National Assembly of South Africa"), the lower house of Parliament, consists of 400 members and is elected every five years by a system of [party-list proportional representation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation "Party-list proportional representation"). The [National Council of Provinces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Council_of_Provinces "National Council of Provinces"), the upper house, consists of ninety members, with each of the nine [provincial legislatures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provincial_legislature_(South_Africa) "Provincial legislature (South Africa)") electing ten members.

After each parliamentary election, the National Assembly elects one of its members as president; hence the president serves a term of office the same as that of the Assembly, normally five years. No president may serve more than two terms in office.<sup id="cite_ref-196"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> The president appoints a [deputy president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deputy_President_of_South_Africa "Deputy President of South Africa") and [ministers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minister_(government) "Minister (government)") (each representing a [department](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_(government_department) "Ministry (government department)")) who form the [cabinet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_South_Africa "Cabinet of South Africa"). The National Assembly may remove the president and the cabinet by a [motion of no confidence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence "Motion of no confidence"). In the [most recent election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_South_African_general_election "2019 South African general election"), held on 8 May 2019, the ANC won 58% of the vote and 230 seats, while the main opposition, the [Democratic Alliance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Alliance_(South_Africa) "Democratic Alliance (South Africa)"), won 21% of the vote and 84 seats. The [Economic Freedom Fighters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_Freedom_Fighters "Economic Freedom Fighters"), founded by [Julius Malema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Malema "Julius Malema"), former president of the [ANC Youth League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_National_Congress_Youth_League "African National Congress Youth League") who was later expelled from the ANC, won 11% of the vote and 44 seats. The ANC has been the governing political party in South Africa since the end of apartheid.<sup id="cite_ref-197"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup>

South Africa has no legally defined capital city. The fourth chapter of the constitution states "The seat of Parliament is Cape Town, but an Act of Parliament enacted in accordance with section 76(1) and (5) may determine that the seat of Parliament is elsewhere."<sup id="cite_ref-198"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> The country's three branches of government are split over different cities. Cape Town, as the seat of Parliament, is the legislative capital; Pretoria, as the seat of the president and cabinet, is the administrative capital; and Bloemfontein is the seat of the [Supreme Court of Appeal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Appeal_(South_Africa) "Supreme Court of Appeal (South Africa)"), and has traditionally been regarded as the judicial capital;<sup id="cite_ref-Marais_Twala_2020_pp._49–62_21-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-Marais_Twala_2020_pp._49%E2%80%9362-21">[21]</a></sup> although the highest court, the [Constitutional Court of South Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa "Constitutional Court of South Africa") has been based in Johannesburg since 1994. Most foreign embassies are located in Pretoria.

Since 2004, South Africa has had many thousands of popular protests,<sup id="cite_ref-199"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> some violent, making it, according to one academic, the "most protest-rich country in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-200"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> There have been numerous incidents of [political repression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_repression_in_post-apartheid_South_Africa "Political repression in post-apartheid South Africa") as well as threats of future repression in violation of the constitution, leading some analysts and [civil society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_society "Civil society") organisations to conclude that there is or could be a new climate of political repression.<sup id="cite_ref-201"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>

In 2022, South Africa placed sixth out of 48 sub-Saharan African countries on the [Ibrahim Index of African Governance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance "Ibrahim Index of African Governance"). South Africa scored well in the categories of [Rule of Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_law "Rule of law"), [Transparency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transparency_(behavior) "Transparency (behavior)") and Corruption, and [Participation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_participation_(decision_making) "Public participation (decision making)") and Human Rights, but score low in Safety and Security.<sup id="cite_ref-203"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (September 2023)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2006, South Africa became the first and only African country to legalise [same-sex marriage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Same-sex_marriage "Same-sex marriage").<sup id="cite_ref-204"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes_27-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-NYTimes-27">[27]</a></sup>

The Constitution of South Africa is the supreme rule of law in the country. The primary sources of [South African law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_South_Africa "Law of South Africa") are [Roman-Dutch mercantile law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman-Dutch_law "Roman-Dutch law") and personal law and [English Common law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_law "English law"), as imports of Dutch settlements and British colonialism.<sup id="cite_ref-205"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> The first European-based law in South Africa was brought by the Dutch East India Company and is called Roman-Dutch law. It was imported before the [codification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Codification_(law) "Codification (law)") of European law into the [Napoleonic Code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_Code "Napoleonic Code") and is comparable in many ways to [Scots law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scots_law "Scots law"). This was followed in the 19th century by English law, both [common](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Common_law "Common law") and [statutory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statutory_law "Statutory law"). After unification in 1910, South Africa had its own parliament which passed laws specific for South Africa, building on those previously passed for the individual member colonies. The judicial system consists of the [magistrates' courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magistrate%27s_court_(South_Africa) "Magistrate's court (South Africa)"), which hear lesser criminal cases and smaller civil cases; the [High Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_Court_of_South_Africa "High Court of South Africa"), which has divisions that serve as the courts of [general jurisdiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_jurisdiction "General jurisdiction") for specific areas; the Supreme Court of Appeal; and the Constitutional Court, which is the highest court.

### Foreign relations

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Leaders_BRICS_summit_2019.jpg/220px-Leaders_BRICS_summit_2019.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Leaders_BRICS_summit_2019.jpg)

President of South Africa, [Cyril Ramaphosa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyril_Ramaphosa "Cyril Ramaphosa") (far left), poses with the [BRICS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BRICS "BRICS") heads of state and government during the [11th BRICS summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/11th_BRICS_summit "11th BRICS summit"), 2019

As the Union of South Africa, the country was a founding member of the United Nations (UN), with Prime Minister [Jan Smuts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Smuts "Jan Smuts") writing the [preamble to the UN Charter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preamble_to_the_United_Nations_Charter "Preamble to the United Nations Charter").<sup id="cite_ref-gildersleeve_206-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-gildersleeve-206">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schlesinger_207-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-Schlesinger-207">[207]</a></sup> South Africa is one of the founding members of the [African Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_Union "African Union") (AU) and has the [third largest economy of all the members](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_GDP_(nominal) "List of African countries by GDP (nominal)"). It is a founding member of the AU's [New Partnership for Africa's Development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development "New Partnership for Africa's Development"). After apartheid ended, South Africa was readmitted to the [Commonwealth of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations "Commonwealth of Nations"). The country is a member of the [Group of 77](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_of_77 "Group of 77") and chaired the organisation in 2006. South Africa is also a member of the [Southern African Development Community](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community "Southern African Development Community"), [South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Atlantic_Peace_and_Cooperation_Zone "South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone"), [Southern African Customs Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_African_Customs_Union "Southern African Customs Union"), [Antarctic Treaty System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_System "Antarctic Treaty System"), [World Trade Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Organization "World Trade Organization"), International Monetary Fund, [G20](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G20 "G20"), [G8+5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G8%2B5 "G8+5"), and the [Port Management Association of Eastern and Southern Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_Management_Association_of_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa "Port Management Association of Eastern and Southern Africa").

South Africa has played a key role as a mediator in African conflicts over the last decade, such as in Burundi, the Democratic Republic of the Congo, Comoros, and Zimbabwe.

President [Jacob Zuma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_Zuma "Jacob Zuma") and Chinese President [Hu Jintao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hu_Jintao "Hu Jintao") upgraded bilateral ties between the two countries in 2010 when they signed the Beijing Agreement which elevated South Africa's earlier "strategic partnership" with China to the higher level of "comprehensive strategic partnership" in both economic and political affairs, including the strengthening of exchanges between their respective ruling parties and legislatures.<sup id="cite_ref-208"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> In 2011, South Africa joined the Brazil-Russia-India-China ([BRICS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BRICS "BRICS")) grouping of countries, identified by Zuma as the country's largest trading partners and also the largest trading partners with Africa as a whole. Zuma asserted that BRICS member countries would also work with each other through the UN, G20, and the India, Brazil South Africa ([IBSA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBSA_Dialogue_Forum "IBSA Dialogue Forum")) forum.<sup id="cite_ref-210"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup>

### Military

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/SAAF-Gripen-001_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-SAAF-Gripen-001_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:SAAF-Gripen-001_(cropped).jpg)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rooivalk_in_flight_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Rooivalk_in_flight_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rooivalk_in_flight_(cropped).jpg)

South African-made [Rooivalk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denel_Rooivalk "Denel Rooivalk") attack helicopter

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/SAS_Spioenkop_during_Exercise_IBSAMAR_V_%28cropped%29.JPG/220px-SAS_Spioenkop_during_Exercise_IBSAMAR_V_%28cropped%29.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:SAS_Spioenkop_during_Exercise_IBSAMAR_V_(cropped).JPG)

The [South African National Defence Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force "South African National Defence Force") (SANDF) was created in 1994<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-1993-224_211-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-constitution-1993-224-211">[211]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> as a [volunteer military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volunteer_military "Volunteer military") composed of the former [South African Defence Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Defence_Force "South African Defence Force"), the forces of the African nationalist groups ([uMkhonto we Sizwe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UMkhonto_we_Sizwe "UMkhonto we Sizwe") and [Azanian People's Liberation Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azanian_People%27s_Liberation_Army "Azanian People's Liberation Army")), and the former Bantustan defence forces.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-1993-224_211-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-constitution-1993-224-211">[211]</a></sup> The SANDF is subdivided into four branches, the [South African Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Army "South African Army"), the [South African Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Air_Force "South African Air Force"), the [South African Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Navy "South African Navy"), and the [South African Military Health Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Military_Health_Service "South African Military Health Service").<sup id="cite_ref-act-42-2002_213-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-act-42-2002-213">[213]</a></sup> The SANDF consists of around 75,000 [professional soldiers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standing_army "Standing army") as of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-214"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> In recent years, the SANDF has become a major [peacekeeping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peacekeeping "Peacekeeping") force in Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-dod-sep2005_215-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-dod-sep2005-215">[215]</a></sup> and has been involved in operations in Lesotho, the DRC,<sup id="cite_ref-dod-sep2005_215-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-dod-sep2005-215">[215]</a></sup> and Burundi,<sup id="cite_ref-dod-sep2005_215-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-dod-sep2005-215">[215]</a></sup> amongst others. It has also served in multinational [UN Peacekeeping forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping "United Nations peacekeeping") such as the [UN Force Intervention Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade "United Nations Force Intervention Brigade"). In 2022 the nation spent US$3.069 billion on its armed forces which is about 0.86% of the nation's entire GDP. Over the years, [defence expenditure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_budget "Military budget") has been cut as the nation currently faces no external military threats.<sup id="cite_ref-216"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup>

The SANDF are often deployed in crime fighting and whenever the [South African Police Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Police_Service "South African Police Service") (SAPS) are no longer able to control the situation.<sup id="cite_ref-217"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> During the [2021 South African unrest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_South_African_unrest "2021 South African unrest"), South Africa's worst violence since the end of [apartheid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apartheid "Apartheid"), saw the deployment of 25,000 troops, more than a dozen military helicopters and heavily armed vehicles deployed in the nation's [KwaZulu-Natal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KwaZulu-Natal "KwaZulu-Natal") and [Gauteng](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gauteng "Gauteng") provinces to assist the South African Police in ending the riots and looting, this was one of the nation's largest military deployments since 1994, the largest deployment of troops since the end of apartheid was in March 2020, when 70,000 troops were deployed to enforce the nation's strict lockdown laws to combat the spread of [COVID-19](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_South_Africa "COVID-19 pandemic in South Africa").<sup id="cite_ref-218"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> South Africa has a lot of [military bases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_South_African_military_bases "List of South African military bases") distributed all over the nation, this includes two naval bases, nine air force bases and the army maintains large bases in all nine provinces of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-219"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup>

The [South African Defence Industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defence_industry_of_South_Africa "Defence industry of South Africa") is the most advanced on the African continent and one of the most advanced in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-220"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> As of 2020 South Africa is the world's 24th largest arms exporter, the only nation in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-222"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> The nation designs many types of weapons that range from armored fighting vehicles to [ballistic missiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ballistic_missile "Ballistic missile"), notable South African-made weapons include the [Ratel IFV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ratel_IFV "Ratel IFV"), the world's first wheeled [infantry fighting vehicle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infantry_fighting_vehicle "Infantry fighting vehicle"), South Africa also made its own [attack helicopter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attack_helicopter "Attack helicopter") known as the "[Rooivalk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denel_Rooivalk "Denel Rooivalk")" which is known to be one of the most advanced attack helicopters in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-223"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> In recent years a R16 billion ($1 billion) contract was signed with the local defence industry which aims to produce 244 units of [Badger IFV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Badger_IFV "Badger IFV") for the SANDF.<sup id="cite_ref-224"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup>

South Africa is the only African country to have successfully developed [nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "South Africa and weapons of mass destruction"). It became the first country (followed by Ukraine) with nuclear capability to voluntarily renounce and dismantle its programme and in the process signed the [Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons "Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons") in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-fas-ocp27_225-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-fas-ocp27-225">[225]</a></sup> South Africa undertook a [nuclear weapons programme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_programme_of_South_Africa "Nuclear programme of South Africa") in the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-fas-ocp27_225-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-fas-ocp27-225">[225]</a></sup> South Africa is [alleged to have conducted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vela_incident "Vela incident") a nuclear test over the Atlantic in 1979,<sup id="cite_ref-226"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> although this is officially denied; de Klerk maintained that South Africa had "never conducted a clandestine nuclear test."<sup id="cite_ref-South_Africa_comes_clean_227-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-South_Africa_comes_clean-227">[227]</a></sup> Six nuclear devices were completed between 1980 and 1990 but all were dismantled by 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-South_Africa_comes_clean_227-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-South_Africa_comes_clean-227">[227]</a></sup> In 2017, South Africa signed the UN treaty on the [Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons "Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons").<sup id="cite_ref-228"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup>

### Law enforcement and crime

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/South_african_police_may_2010.jpg/220px-South_african_police_may_2010.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:South_african_police_may_2010.jpg)

Officers of the [South African Police Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Police_Service "South African Police Service") with [Vektor R5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R4_assault_rifle "R4 assault rifle") rifles on parade in Johannesburg, 2010

Law enforcement in South Africa is primarily the responsibility of the [South African Police Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Police_Service "South African Police Service") (SAPS), South Africa's national police force. SAPS is responsible for investigating crime and security throughout the country. The South African Police Service has over 1,154 police stations across the country and over 150,950 officers.<sup id="cite_ref-229"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> In 2023 the [Special Task Force (SAPS)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Task_Force_(SAPS) "Special Task Force (SAPS)") placed 9th at the international SWAT competition out of 55 law enforcement teams from across the world making it the best in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-230"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup>

South Africa has the world's largest [private security industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_security_industry_in_South_Africa "Private security industry in South Africa"),<sup id="cite_ref-231"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> with over 10,380 private security companies and 2.5 million private security personnel of which over 556,000 are active,<sup id="cite_ref-232"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> making it bigger than the South African Police Force and Military combined.<sup id="cite_ref-233"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Private security mainly provide assistance to the South African Police Service (SAPS) to combat crime throughout the country. Over the years there has been tremendous growth in the private security industry.<sup id="cite_ref-234"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup>

As of February 2023, South Africa has the sixth highest crime rate in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-235"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> From April 2017 to March 2018, on average 57 murders were committed each day in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-236"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> In the year ended March 2017, there were 20,336 murders and the murder rate was 35.9 per 100,000 – over five times higher than the global average of 6.2 per 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-237"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> More than 526,000 South Africans were murdered from 1994 to 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-238"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Smash_and_Grab_Hot_Spot%2C_Retreat_%28South_Africa%29.jpg/220px-Smash_and_Grab_Hot_Spot%2C_Retreat_%28South_Africa%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Smash_and_Grab_Hot_Spot,_Retreat_(South_Africa).jpg)

Smash and Grab Hot Spot sign in [Retreat, Cape Town](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retreat,_Cape_Town "Retreat, Cape Town")

South Africa has a high rape rate, with 43,195 rapes reported in 2014/15, and an unknown number of [sexual assaults](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_assault "Sexual assault") going unreported.<sup id="cite_ref-africaCheckRapeStats_239-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-africaCheckRapeStats-239">[239]</a></sup> A 2009 survey of 1,738 men in KwaZulu-Natal and the Eastern Cape by the Medical Research Council found one in four men admitted to raping someone,<sup id="cite_ref-240"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> and another survey of 4,000 women in Johannesburg by CIET Africa found one in three said they had been raped in the past year.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1_241-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-bbc1-241">[241]</a></sup> Rape occurs most commonly within relationships, but many men and women say that rape cannot occur in relationships; however, one in four women reported having been abused by an intimate partner.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrahams_242-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-Abrahams-242">[242]</a></sup> Rapes are also perpetrated by children (some as young as ten).<sup id="cite_ref-medscape_243-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-medscape-243">[243]</a></sup> The incidence of [child and infant rape](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse "Child sexual abuse") is among the highest in the world, largely as a result of the [virgin cleansing myth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgin_cleansing_myth "Virgin cleansing myth"), and a number of high-profile cases (sometimes as young as eight months)<sup id="cite_ref-medscape_243-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-medscape-243">[243]</a></sup> have outraged the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-time_244-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-time-244">[244]</a></sup>

Between 1994 and 2018, there were more than 500 [xenophobic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xenophobia "Xenophobia") [attacks against foreigners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xenophobia_in_South_Africa "Xenophobia in South Africa") in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-245"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> The [2019 Johannesburg riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Johannesburg_riots "2019 Johannesburg riots") were similar in nature and origin to the [2008 xenophobic riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/May_2008_South_Africa_riots "May 2008 South Africa riots") that also occurred in Johannesburg.<sup id="cite_ref-246"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup>

### Administrative divisions

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg/350px-Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg)

[Provinces of South Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provinces_of_South_Africa "Provinces of South Africa")

Each of the nine provinces is governed by a [unicameral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicameralism "Unicameralism") [legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provincial_legislature_(South_Africa) "Provincial legislature (South Africa)"), which is elected every five years by [party-list proportional representation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation "Party-list proportional representation"). The legislature elects a [premier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Premier_(South_Africa) "Premier (South Africa)") as head of government, and the premier appoints an [Executive Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Council_(South_Africa) "Executive Council (South Africa)") as a provincial cabinet. The powers of provincial governments are limited to topics listed in the constitution; these topics include such fields as health, education, public housing and transport.

The provinces are in turn divided into 52 [districts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Districts_of_South_Africa "Districts of South Africa"): 8 [metropolitan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_municipality_(South_Africa) "Metropolitan municipality (South Africa)") and 44 [district municipalities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/District_municipality_(South_Africa) "District municipality (South Africa)"). The district municipalities are further subdivided into 205 [local municipalities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_municipality_(South_Africa) "Local municipality (South Africa)"). The metropolitan municipalities, which govern the largest urban agglomerations, perform the functions of both district and local municipalities.

| [Free State](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_State_(South_African_province) "Free State (South African province)") | [Bloemfontein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloemfontein "Bloemfontein") | Bloemfontein | 129,825 | 2,834,714 | 2,929,000 |
| [Gauteng](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gauteng "Gauteng") | [Johannesburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannesburg "Johannesburg") | Johannesburg | 18,178 | 13,399,724 | 15,488,000 |
