| [Northern Cape](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Cape "Northern Cape") | [Kimberley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kimberley,_South_Africa "Kimberley, South Africa") | Kimberley | 372,889 | 1,193,780 | 1,293,000 |
| [Western Cape](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Cape "Western Cape") | [Cape Town](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Town "Cape Town") | Cape Town | 129,462 | 6,279,730 | 7,006,000 |

## Economy

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg/170px-Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg)

The [Johannesburg Stock Exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JSE_Limited "JSE Limited") (JSE) is the largest [stock exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stock_exchange "Stock exchange") on the African continent and the [17th largest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges "List of stock exchanges") in the world with a [market capitalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Market_capitalization "Market capitalization") of $1.36 trillion<sup id="cite_ref-250"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup>

South Africa has a [mixed economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixed_economy "Mixed economy"), South Africa's economy is the most industrialized and technologically advanced in Africa respectively,<sup id="cite_ref-251"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> it has the [second largest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_GDP_(nominal) "List of African countries by GDP (nominal)") economy in Africa, after Nigeria and the [39th largest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)") in the world. It also has a relatively high gross domestic product (GDP) per capita compared to other countries in sub-Saharan Africa US$16,080 at [purchasing power parity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity "Purchasing power parity") as of 2023 ranked 95th. Despite this, South Africa is still burdened by a relatively high rate of poverty and unemployment and is ranked in the top ten countries in the world for [income inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_inequality "Economic inequality"),<sup id="cite_ref-252"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> measured by the [Gini coefficient](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gini_coefficient "Gini coefficient").

South Africa is ranked 40th by [total Wealth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_total_wealth "List of countries by total wealth"), making it the second wealthiest country in Africa, in terms of private wealth South Africa has a private wealth of $651 billion making South Africa's population the richest in Africa followed by [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt") with $307 billion and [Nigeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nigeria "Nigeria") with $228 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-255"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup>

Approximately 55.5% (30.3 million people) of the population is living in poverty at the national upper [poverty line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poverty_threshold "Poverty threshold") while a total of 13.8 million people (25% of the population) are experiencing food poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-256"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup>

In 2015, 71% of net wealth are held by 10% of the population, whereas 60% of the population held only 7% of the net wealth, and the Gini coefficient was 0.63, whereas in 1996 it was 0.61.<sup id="cite_ref-257"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup>

Unlike most of the world's poor countries, South Africa does not have a thriving [informal economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Informal_economy "Informal economy"). Only 15% of South African jobs are in the [informal sector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Informal_economy "Informal economy"), compared with around half in [Brazil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil "Economy of Brazil") and [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_India "Economy of India") and nearly three-quarters in [Indonesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Indonesia "Economy of Indonesia"). The Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development ([OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD")) attributes this difference to South Africa's widespread welfare system.<sup id="cite_ref-economist1_258-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-economist1-258">[258]</a></sup> [World Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank "World Bank") research shows that South Africa has one of the widest gaps between per capita GDP versus its [Human Development Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Development_Index "Human Development Index") ranking, with only Botswana showing a larger gap.<sup id="cite_ref-259"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Johannesburg_Skyline.jpg/220px-Johannesburg_Skyline.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Johannesburg_Skyline.jpg)

[Johannesburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannesburg "Johannesburg"), the financial capital of South Africa and the African continent<sup id="cite_ref-260"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup>

After 1994, government policy brought down inflation, stabilised public finances, and some foreign capital was attracted; however, growth was still subpar.<sup id="cite_ref-assessment2008-2_261-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-assessment2008-2-261">[261]</a></sup> From 2004 onward, economic growth picked up significantly; both employment and [capital formation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_formation "Capital formation") increased.<sup id="cite_ref-assessment2008-2_261-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-assessment2008-2-261">[261]</a></sup> During the presidency of [Jacob Zuma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_Zuma "Jacob Zuma"), the government increased the role of [state-owned enterprises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State-owned_enterprise "State-owned enterprise") (SOEs). Some of the biggest SOEs are [Eskom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eskom "Eskom"), the electric power monopoly, [South African Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Airways "South African Airways") (SAA), and [Transnet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transnet "Transnet"), the railroad and ports monopoly. Some of these SOEs have not been profitable, such as SAA, which has required bailouts totaling R30 billion ($2.03 billion) over the 20 years preceding 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-262"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> Principal international trading partners of South Africa—besides other African countries—include Germany, the United States, China, Japan, the United Kingdom and Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_167-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-factbook-167">[167]</a></sup> The 2020 [Financial Secrecy Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_Secrecy_Index "Financial Secrecy Index") ranked South Africa as the 58th safest [tax haven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_haven "Tax haven") in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-263"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup>

The [South African agricultural industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agriculture_in_South_Africa "Agriculture in South Africa") contributes around 10% of formal employment, relatively low compared to other parts of Africa, as well as providing work for casual labourers and contributing around 2.6% of GDP for the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_264-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-HRW-264">[264]</a></sup> Due to the [aridity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arid "Arid") of the land, only 13.5% can be used for crop production, and only 3% is considered high potential land.<sup id="cite_ref-265"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup>

In August 2013, South Africa was ranked as the top African Country of the Future by _[fDi Intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FDi_Intelligence "FDi Intelligence")_ based on the country's [economic potential](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_potential "Economic potential"), labour environment, cost-effectiveness, infrastructure, business friendliness, and [foreign direct investment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment "Foreign direct investment") strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-266"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup>

### Mining

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Platinum_Mining.jpg/220px-Platinum_Mining.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Platinum_Mining.jpg)

An aerial view of the [Two Rivers mine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Two_Rivers_mine "Two Rivers mine") in [Steelpoort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steelpoort "Steelpoort"), [Limpopo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limpopo "Limpopo"), owned by both African Rainbow Minerals and Impala Platinum holdings limited.

South Africa has always been a mining powerhouse. Until 2006 South Africa was the [world's largest gold producer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_gold_production "List of countries by gold production") for almost a century, by the end of 2009 gold mining in South Africa had declined rapidly having produced 205 metric tons (mt) of gold in 2008 compared to 1,000 metric tons produced in 1970 (almost 80% of the world's mine supply at the time).<sup id="cite_ref-267"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> Despite this, the country still has 6,000 tonnes of gold reserves<sup id="cite_ref-268"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> and is still number 5 in gold production and remains a cornucopia of mineral riches.<sup id="cite_ref-269"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> South Africa is home to worlds deepest gold mine, [Mponeng Gold Mine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mponeng_Gold_Mine "Mponeng Gold Mine"), reaching nearly 4000m depth. <sup id="cite_ref-270"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup>It is the world's largest producer<sup id="cite_ref-auto_271-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-auto-271">[271]</a></sup> of [chrome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromium "Chromium"), [manganese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manganese "Manganese"), [platinum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Platinum "Platinum"), [vanadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanadium "Vanadium") and [vermiculite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vermiculite "Vermiculite"). It is the second largest producer<sup id="cite_ref-auto_271-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-auto-271">[271]</a></sup> of [ilmenite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilmenite "Ilmenite"), [palladium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palladium "Palladium"), [rutile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rutile "Rutile") and [zirconium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zirconium "Zirconium"). It is the world's third largest coal exporter.<sup id="cite_ref-platts.com_272-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-platts.com-272">[272]</a></sup> It is a huge producer of iron ore; in 2012, it overtook India to become the world's third-biggest iron ore supplier to China, the world's largest consumers of iron ore.<sup id="cite_ref-mwsa_273-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-mwsa-273">[273]</a></sup>

### Tourism

[![A straight stone pathway through a rocky area, elevated in places from the walkway, with a low retaining wall and chain fence on the left. Beyond is an area of ocean; at the far background on the left is a large flat rocky mountain with a peaked one at its left. Closer to the camera is a small building on the right; people are milling around it and the paths, some taking pictures](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Tourists_looking_at_Table_Mountain_and_Cape_Town_from_viewpoint_on_Robben_Island.jpg/220px-Tourists_looking_at_Table_Mountain_and_Cape_Town_from_viewpoint_on_Robben_Island.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tourists_looking_at_Table_Mountain_and_Cape_Town_from_viewpoint_on_Robben_Island.jpg)

Tourists taking in the view of Cape Town and Table Mountain from [Robben Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robben_Island "Robben Island")

South Africa is a [tourist destination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tourist_destination "Tourist destination") with the tourist industry accounting for 2.34% of GDP<sup id="cite_ref-Tourism_in_South_Africa_:3_274-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-Tourism_in_South_Africa_:3-274">[274]</a></sup> in 2019 followed by a sharp drop in 2020 to 0.81% of GDP<sup id="cite_ref-Tourism_in_South_Africa_:3_274-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-Tourism_in_South_Africa_:3-274">[274]</a></sup> due to lack of travel caused by the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic"). The official marketing agency for the country [South African Tourism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Tourism "South African Tourism") is responsible for marketing South Africa to the world. According to the World Travel & Tourism Council, the tourism industry directly contributed [ZAR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_rand "South African rand") 102 billion to South African [GDP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GDP "GDP") in 2012, and supports 10.3% of jobs in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-275"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> The official national [marketing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marketing "Marketing") agency of the South African government, with the goal of promoting tourism in South Africa both locally and globally is known as [South African Tourism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Tourism "South African Tourism").<sup id="cite_ref-276"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup>

South Africa offers both domestic and international tourists a wide variety of options, among others the [picturesque natural landscape](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_South_Africa "Geography of South Africa") and [game reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SANParks "SANParks"), diverse [cultural heritage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_South_Africa "Culture of South Africa") and [highly regarded wines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_wine "South African wine"). Some of the most popular destinations include several national parks, such as the expansive [Kruger National Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kruger_National_Park "Kruger National Park") in the north of the country, the coastlines and beaches of the [KwaZulu-Natal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KwaZulu-Natal "KwaZulu-Natal") and [Western Cape](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Cape "Western Cape") provinces, and the major cities like [Cape Town](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Town "Cape Town"), [Johannesburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannesburg "Johannesburg") and [Durban](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durban "Durban").

According to Statistics South Africa's latest Tourism and Migration Survey, almost 3,5 million travellers passed through the country's ports of entry in August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-277"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> The top five overseas countries with the largest number of tourists visiting South Africa were the [US](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States"), [UK](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom"), [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany "Germany"), the [Netherlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netherlands "Netherlands") and [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France "France"). Most of the tourists arriving in South Africa from elsewhere in Africa came from [SADC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community "Southern African Development Community") countries. [Zimbabwe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zimbabwe "Zimbabwe") tops the list at 31%, followed by [Lesotho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lesotho "Lesotho"), [Mozambique](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozambique "Mozambique"), [Eswatini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eswatini "Eswatini") and [Botswana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Botswana "Botswana"). In addition, Nigeria was the country of origin for nearly 30% of tourists arriving in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-278"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup>

## Infrastructure

### Roads

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Mandela_Bridge%2C_Johannesburg%2C_Gauteng%2C_South_Africa.jpg/220px-Mandela_Bridge%2C_Johannesburg%2C_Gauteng%2C_South_Africa.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mandela_Bridge,_Johannesburg,_Gauteng,_South_Africa.jpg)

The [Nelson Mandela Bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_Bridge "Nelson Mandela Bridge") in [Johannesburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannesburg "Johannesburg")

South Africa has a total road network of 750,000 kilometres, the largest of any African country and the [12th largest in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_road_network_size "List of countries by road network size"). According to [SANRAL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SANRAL "SANRAL"), the road network is valued at more than R2.1 trillion. SANRAL manages national roads and has a network of 22 197 kilometres of paved roads. Provinces are responsible for 222 951 kilometres while, according to the DoT, the municipal network is estimated at 275 661 kilometres of the proclaimed network. The rest are unproclaimed gravel roads (mainly serving rural communities) and are therefore not owned or maintained by any road authority. The country has more than 12 million motor vehicles with an average density of 16 motor vehicles per kilometre. The provincial road network is about 222 951 kilometres in length, consisting of 170 837 kilometres of unpaved and 52 114 kilometres of paved roads.<sup id="cite_ref-279"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup>

### Railways

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Gautrain...%2C_O_R_Tambo_Intl_Airport_South_Africa.jpg/220px-Gautrain...%2C_O_R_Tambo_Intl_Airport_South_Africa.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Gautrain...,_O_R_Tambo_Intl_Airport_South_Africa.jpg)

[Gautrain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gautrain "Gautrain") [higher-speed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Higher-speed_rail "Higher-speed rail") commuter rail

Rail transport in South Africa is an important element of the country's [transport infrastructure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transportation_infrastructure "Transportation infrastructure"). All major cities are connected by rail. [Transnet Freight Rail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transnet_Freight_Rail "Transnet Freight Rail") mainly operates freight services while [PRASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passenger_Rail_Agency_of_South_Africa "Passenger Rail Agency of South Africa") operates commuter services. State-owned utility Transnet Freight Rail is the largest freight rail transport operator on the African continent, the company maintains a rail network of approximately 31,000 kilometres but only 20,900 kilometres of this are in use.<sup id="cite_ref-280"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup>

South Africa's railway system is the most developed and largest in Africa as well as the [13th largest in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_rail_transport_network_size "List of countries by rail transport network size"); however, vandalism, theft, and underinvestment has left left the overall condition of the majority of networks in a poor state.<sup id="cite_ref-281"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> Freight, passenger and port capacity shortages remain a severe constraint in domestic and regional trade.<sup id="cite_ref-282"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> Coal and iron ore are mainly transported on these lines, the country's rail network carried nearly 230 million tons of freight in 2017 however, this has declined to 179 million tons in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup>and it is likely that efforts will be made to revitalize the these transport sectors through private sector partnerships.<sup id="cite_ref-284"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup>

### Airports

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/South_African_Airways_Airbus_A340-313_ZS-SXE_MUC_2015_01.jpg/220px-South_African_Airways_Airbus_A340-313_ZS-SXE_MUC_2015_01.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:South_African_Airways_Airbus_A340-313_ZS-SXE_MUC_2015_01.jpg)

[South African Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_Airways "South African Airways") [Airbus A340](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airbus_A340 "Airbus A340") at [Munich Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich_Airport "Munich Airport")

South Africa has international airports in six cities: [Johannesburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannesburg "Johannesburg"), [Cape Town](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Town "Cape Town"), [Durban](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durban "Durban"), [Port Elizabeth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gqeberha "Gqeberha"), [Kimberley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kimberley_Airport "Kimberley Airport") and [Nelspruit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nelspruit_Airport "Nelspruit Airport").<sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup>

As of 2021, South Africa had 407 airports, making it the leading country in Africa in terms of airport ownership and the country ranked 20th globally.<sup id="cite_ref-286"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup>

The four [major](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_South_African_airports_by_passenger_movements "List of South African airports by passenger movements") airports in South Africa are: [O.R. Tambo International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/O._R._Tambo_International_Airport "O. R. Tambo International Airport") in Johannesburg, [Cape Town International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Town_International_Airport "Cape Town International Airport"), [King Shaka International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_Shaka_International_Airport "King Shaka International Airport") in Durban and [Chief Dawid Stuurman International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Dawid_Stuurman_International_Airport "Chief Dawid Stuurman International Airport") in Port Elizabeth.

O.R. Tambo International Airport in Johannesburg is Africa's largest and busiest airport which receives over 21 million passengers a year.<sup id="cite_ref-287"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> During the 2022 [Skytrax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skytrax "Skytrax") World Airport Awards, Cape Town International Airport was voted the best airport on the African continent for the seventh consecutive year, Durban's King Shaka International Airport was voted the second best in Africa and Johannesburg's O.R. Tambo International Airport came third place.<sup id="cite_ref-288"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup>

### Energy

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Koebergnps.jpg/220px-Koebergnps.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Koebergnps.jpg)

The [Koeberg Power Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koeberg_Nuclear_Power_Station "Koeberg Nuclear Power Station"), the only [nuclear power plant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant "Nuclear power plant") on the entire African continent

South Africa has a very large energy sector and is currently the only country on the African continent that possesses a [nuclear power plant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koeberg_Nuclear_Power_Station "Koeberg Nuclear Power Station").<sup id="cite_ref-289"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup> The country is the largest producer of electricity on the African continent and it ranks 21st globally.<sup id="cite_ref-290"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> South Africa is the [7th largest coal producer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_coal_production "List of countries by coal production") in the world and produces in excess of 248 million [tonnes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tonne "Tonne") of [coal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coal "Coal") and consumes almost three-quarters of that domestically. Around 77% of South Africa's energy needs are directly derived from coal and 92% of coal consumed on the African continent is mined in South Africa. South Africa is also the world's 14th largest emitter of [greenhouse gases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_gas "Greenhouse gas").<sup id="cite_ref-291"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup>

The country's primary electricity generator is Eskom, the utility is the largest producer of electricity in [Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Africa "Africa"), and is among the top seven utilities in the world in terms of generation capacity and among the top nine in terms of sales.<sup id="cite_ref-as_292-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-as-292">[292]</a></sup> It is the largest of [South Africa's state owned enterprises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State-owned_enterprises_of_South_Africa "State-owned enterprises of South Africa"). Eskom generates approximately 95% of electricity in South Africa and operates a number of notable [power stations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_station "Power station"), including the [Koeberg Nuclear Power Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koeberg_Nuclear_Power_Station "Koeberg Nuclear Power Station") in Cape Town, the only nuclear power plant in Africa, [Kendal Power Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kendal_Power_Station "Kendal Power Station"), the largest dry-cooled power station in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> as well as [Duvha Power Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duvha_Power_Station "Duvha Power Station") which became the first power station in the world to be retrofitted with [pulse jet fabric filter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dust_collector#Reverse_jet "Dust collector") plants.<sup id="cite_ref-294"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> In 2001 Eskom was named the best electricity utility in the entire world.<sup id="cite_ref-as_292-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-as-292">[292]</a></sup>

#### Energy crisis

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Kusilekragsentrale%2C_Mpumalanga%2C_2019%2C_a.jpg/220px-Kusilekragsentrale%2C_Mpumalanga%2C_2019%2C_a.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kusilekragsentrale,_Mpumalanga,_2019,_a.jpg)

The [Kusile Power Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kusile_Power_Station "Kusile Power Station") was built as a response to the energy crisis. When fully operational it will be the 4th largest [coal-fired power station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coal-fired_power_station "Coal-fired power station") in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-295"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup>

Due to severe mismanagement and [corruption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corruption_in_South_Africa "Corruption in South Africa") at Eskom, the company is R392bn ($22bn) in debt and is unable to meet the demands of the South African power grid.<sup id="cite_ref-296"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> Due to this, Eskom implemented [loadshedding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loadshedding "Loadshedding"), which is periodically switching off electricity to specific power grids in specific time frames. In South Africa, load shedding is done to prevent a failure of the entire system when the demand for electricity strains the capacity of Eskom's power generating system. Load shedding is characterized by periods of widespread national-level rolling blackouts.<sup id="cite_ref-297"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> Eskom's latest energy availability factor (EAF) data reveals that mismanagement, corruption, poor maintenance, and sabotage caused power station breakdowns.<sup id="cite_ref-298"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> In 2023 the [South African Military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force "South African National Defence Force") was deployed to protect Eskom's power stations from sabotage and theft.<sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup>

In 2007 Eskom started the construction of the "[Kusile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kusile_Power_Station "Kusile Power Station")" and "[Medupi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medupi_Power_Station "Medupi Power Station")" power stations, the two mega power stations will be the largest dry-cooled power stations in the world and among the largest power stations in the world scheduled for completion in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-300"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> However, these power stations have never met their deadline date with only half of their six units completed and operational mainly caused by long delays and massive cost overruns exceeding more than R300 billion ($16bn) for the two power stations combined, and are only expected to be completed by 2024 or 2026.<sup id="cite_ref-301"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup>

### Science and technology

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg/220px-Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg)

[Mark Shuttleworth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Shuttleworth "Mark Shuttleworth") in space

Several important scientific and technological developments have originated in South Africa. South Africa was ranked 59th in the [Global Innovation Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index "Global Innovation Index") in 2023, up from 63rd in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-302"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> The first human-to-human [heart transplant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heart_transplantation "Heart transplantation") was performed by cardiac surgeon [Christiaan Barnard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christiaan_Barnard "Christiaan Barnard") at [Groote Schuur Hospital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groote_Schuur_Hospital "Groote Schuur Hospital") in December 1967; [Max Theiler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Theiler "Max Theiler") developed a [vaccine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_fever_vaccine "Yellow fever vaccine") against [yellow fever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_fever "Yellow fever"), [Allan MacLeod Cormack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allan_MacLeod_Cormack "Allan MacLeod Cormack") pioneered X-ray computed tomography ([CT scan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CT_scan "CT scan")); and [Aaron Klug](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aaron_Klug "Aaron Klug") developed [crystallographic electron microscopy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_crystallography "Electron crystallography") techniques. Cormack and Klug received [Nobel Prizes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize "Nobel Prize") for their work. [Sydney Brenner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sydney_Brenner "Sydney Brenner") won in 2002, for his pioneering work in [molecular biology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_biology "Molecular biology"). [Mark Shuttleworth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Shuttleworth "Mark Shuttleworth") founded an early Internet security company [Thawte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thawte "Thawte").<sup id="cite_ref-305"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup>

South Africa has cultivated a burgeoning [astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomy "Astronomy") community. It hosts the [Southern African Large Telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_African_Large_Telescope "Southern African Large Telescope"), the largest [optical telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_telescope "Optical telescope") in the [Southern Hemisphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere "Southern Hemisphere"). South Africa is currently building the [Karoo Array Telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MeerKAT "MeerKAT") as a pathfinder for the €1.5 billion [Square Kilometre Array](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Square_Kilometre_Array "Square Kilometre Array") project.<sup id="cite_ref-306"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup>

### Transport

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/MyCiti_Bus_system_Civic_Centre_station_2.JPG/220px-MyCiti_Bus_system_Civic_Centre_station_2.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:MyCiti_Bus_system_Civic_Centre_station_2.JPG)

[MyCiTi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MyCiTi "MyCiTi") Bus in [Cape Town](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Town "Cape Town")

Modes of transport include roads, railways, airports, water, and pipelines for petroleum oil. The majority of people in South Africa use informal [minibus taxis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Share_taxi "Share taxi") as their main mode of transport. [Bus rapid transit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit "Bus rapid transit") has been implemented in some cities in an attempt to provide more formalised and safer public transport services. These systems have been widely criticised<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (February 2024)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> because of their large capital and operating costs. South Africa has many major ports including Cape Town, Durban, and Port Elizabeth that allow ships and other boats to pass through, some carrying passengers and some carrying [petroleum tankers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_tanker "Oil tanker").

### Water supply and sanitation

Two distinctive features of the South African water sector are the policy of free basic water and the existence of [water boards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_Board_(South_Africa) "Water Board (South Africa)"), which are bulk water supply agencies that operate pipelines and sell water from reservoirs to municipalities. These features have led to significant problems concerning the financial sustainability of service providers, leading to a lack of attention to maintenance. Following the end of apartheid, the country had made improvements in the levels of access to water as those with access increased from 66% to 79% from 1990 to 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-JMP_307-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-JMP-307">[307]</a></sup> Sanitation access increased from 71% to 79% during the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-JMP_307-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-JMP-307">[307]</a></sup> However, water supply and sanitation has come under increasing pressure in recent years despite a commitment made by the government to improve service standards and provide investment subsidies to the water industry.<sup id="cite_ref-308"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup>

The eastern parts of South Africa suffer from periodic droughts linked to the [El Niño](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o "El Niño") weather phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation_309-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation-309">[309]</a></sup> In early 2018, Cape Town, which has different weather patterns to the rest of the country,<sup id="cite_ref-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation_309-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation-309">[309]</a></sup> faced a water crisis as the city's water supply was predicted to run dry before the end of June. Water-saving measures were in effect that required each citizen to use less than 50 litres (13 US gal) per day.<sup id="cite_ref-310"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup> Cape Town rejected an offer from Israel to help it build [desalination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desalination "Desalination") plants.<sup id="cite_ref-311"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-312"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-313"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup>

## Culture

The South African black majority still has a substantial number of rural inhabitants who lead largely impoverished lives. It is among these people that cultural traditions survive most strongly; as blacks have become increasingly urbanised and [Westernised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_world "Western world"), aspects of traditional culture have declined. Members of the middle class, who have historically been predominantly white but whose ranks include growing numbers of Black, Coloured and Indian people,<sup id="cite_ref-315"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> have lifestyles similar in many respects to that of people found in Western Europe, North America and [Australasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australasia "Australasia").

### Arts

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/San_Rock_Art_-_Cederberg.jpg/220px-San_Rock_Art_-_Cederberg.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:San_Rock_Art_-_Cederberg.jpg)

[Rock painting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rock_art "Rock art") by the [San people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_people "San people"), [Cederberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cederberg "Cederberg")

[South African art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_art "South African art") includes the oldest art objects in the world, which were discovered in a South African cave and dated from roughly 75,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-317"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> The scattered tribes of the Khoisan peoples moving into South Africa from around 10,000 BC had their own fluent art styles seen today in a multitude of cave paintings. They were superseded by the Bantu/Nguni peoples with their own vocabularies of art forms. Forms of art evolved in the mines and townships: a dynamic art using everything from plastic strips to bicycle spokes. The Dutch-influenced folk art of the Afrikaner [_trekboers_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trekboer "Trekboer") and the urban white artists, earnestly following changing European traditions from the 1850s onwards, also contributed to this eclectic mix which continues to evolve to this day.

### Popular culture

The [South African media](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_media_in_South_Africa "Mass media in South Africa") sector is large, and South Africa is one of Africa's major media centres. While the many broadcasters and publications reflect the diversity of the population as a whole, the most commonly used language is English. However, all ten other official languages are represented to some extent or another.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2014-11-26_traditional_Zulu_performance_02_anagoria.JPG/220px-2014-11-26_traditional_Zulu_performance_02_anagoria.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2014-11-26_traditional_Zulu_performance_02_anagoria.JPG)

[Zulus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zulus "Zulus") performing a traditional dance

There is great diversity in [South African music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_of_South_Africa "Music of South Africa"). Black musicians have developed unique styles called [Kwaito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kwaito "Kwaito") and [Amapiano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amapiano "Amapiano"), that is said to have taken over radio, television, and magazines.<sup id="cite_ref-318"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> Of note is [Brenda Fassie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brenda_Fassie "Brenda Fassie"), who launched to fame with her song "[Weekend Special](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weekend_Special "Weekend Special")", which was sung in English. More famous traditional musicians include [Ladysmith Black Mambazo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ladysmith_Black_Mambazo "Ladysmith Black Mambazo"), while the [Soweto String Quartet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soweto_String_Quartet "Soweto String Quartet") performs classical music with an African flavour. South Africa has produced world-famous jazz musicians, notably [Hugh Masekela](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugh_Masekela "Hugh Masekela"), [Jonas Gwangwa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonas_Gwangwa "Jonas Gwangwa"), [Abdullah Ibrahim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_Ibrahim "Abdullah Ibrahim"), [Miriam Makeba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miriam_Makeba "Miriam Makeba"), [Jonathan Butler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Butler "Jonathan Butler"), [Chris McGregor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_McGregor "Chris McGregor"), and [Sathima Bea Benjamin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sathima_Bea_Benjamin "Sathima Bea Benjamin"). Afrikaans music covers multiple genres, such as the contemporary [Steve Hofmeyr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Hofmeyr "Steve Hofmeyr"), the [punk rock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punk_rock "Punk rock") band [Fokofpolisiekar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fokofpolisiekar "Fokofpolisiekar"), and the singer-songwriter [Jeremy Loops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremy_Loops "Jeremy Loops"). South African popular musicians that have found international success include [Manfred Mann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manfred_Mann_(musician) "Manfred Mann (musician)"), [Johnny Clegg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnny_Clegg "Johnny Clegg"), rap-rave duo [Die Antwoord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Die_Antwoord "Die Antwoord"), rock band [Seether](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seether "Seether") and rappers such as [AKA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AKA_(rapper) "AKA (rapper)"), [Nasty C](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasty_C "Nasty C") and [Cassper Nyovest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cassper_Nyovest "Cassper Nyovest") gained notoriety in other avenues like the BET Awards for best African acts.

Although few [South African film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinema_of_South_Africa "Cinema of South Africa") productions are known outside South Africa, many foreign films have been produced about South Africa. Arguably, the most high-profile film portraying South Africa in recent years was _[District 9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/District_9 "District 9")_ and its upcoming sequel, as well as _[Chappie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chappie_(film) "Chappie (film)")_. Other notable exceptions are the film _[Tsotsi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsotsi "Tsotsi")_, which won the [Academy Award for Foreign Language Film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_International_Feature_Film "Academy Award for Best International Feature Film") at the [78th Academy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/78th_Academy_Awards "78th Academy Awards") in 2006, as well as _[U-Carmen e-Khayelitsha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U-Carmen_e-Khayelitsha "U-Carmen e-Khayelitsha")_, which won the [Golden Bear](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Bear "Golden Bear") at the 2005 [Berlin International Film Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_International_Film_Festival "Berlin International Film Festival"). In 2015, the [Oliver Hermanus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oliver_Hermanus "Oliver Hermanus") film [_The Endless River_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Endless_River_(film) "The Endless River (film)") became the first South African film selected for the [Venice Film Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival "Venice Film Festival").

### Literature

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Alan_Paton.jpg/170px-Alan_Paton.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Alan_Paton.jpg)

[Alan Paton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Paton "Alan Paton"), [anti-apartheid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_resistance_to_apartheid "Internal resistance to apartheid") activist and writer

[South African literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_literature "South African literature") emerged from a unique social and political history. One of the first well known novels written by a black author in an African language was [Solomon Thekiso Plaatje](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sol_Plaatje "Sol Plaatje")'s _[Mhudi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mhudi "Mhudi")_, written in 1930. During the 1950s, _[Drum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drum_(South_African_magazine) "Drum (South African magazine)")_ magazine became a hotbed of political satire, fiction, and essays, giving a voice to the urban black culture.

Notable white South African authors include [Alan Paton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Paton "Alan Paton"), who published the novel _[Cry, the Beloved Country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cry,_the_Beloved_Country "Cry, the Beloved Country")_ in 1948. [Nadine Gordimer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nadine_Gordimer "Nadine Gordimer") became the first South African to be awarded the [Nobel Prize in Literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature "Nobel Prize in Literature"), in 1991. [J.M. Coetzee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._M._Coetzee "J. M. Coetzee") won the Nobel Prize in Literature in 2003. When awarding the prize, the [Swedish Academy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedish_Academy "Swedish Academy") stated that Coetzee "in innumerable guises portrays the surprising involvement of the outsider."<sup id="cite_ref-Swedish_Academy_319-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-Swedish_Academy-319">[319]</a></sup>

The plays of [Athol Fugard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Athol_Fugard "Athol Fugard") have been regularly premiered in [fringe theatres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fringe_theatre "Fringe theatre") in South Africa, London ([Royal Court Theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Court_Theatre "Royal Court Theatre")) and New York. [Olive Schreiner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olive_Schreiner "Olive Schreiner")'s _[The Story of an African Farm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Story_of_an_African_Farm "The Story of an African Farm")_ (1883) was a revelation in [Victorian literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victorian_literature "Victorian literature"): it is heralded by many as introducing feminism into the novel form.

[Breyten Breytenbach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breyten_Breytenbach "Breyten Breytenbach") was jailed for his involvement with the guerrilla movement against apartheid. [André Brink](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Brink "André Brink") was the first Afrikaner writer to be [banned](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banned_book "Banned book") by the government after he released the novel _[A Dry White Season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_Dry_White_Season_(novel) "A Dry White Season (novel)")_.

### Cuisine

The cuisine of South Africa is diverse, and foods from many different cultures and backgrounds are enjoyed by all communities, and especially marketed to tourists who wish to sample the large variety available. The cuisine is mostly meat-based and has spawned the distinctively South African social gathering known as the _[braai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braai "Braai")_, a variation of the [barbecue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barbecue "Barbecue"). South Africa has also developed into a major [wine producer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_African_wine "South African wine"), with some of the best [vineyards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vineyard "Vineyard") lying in valleys around [Stellenbosch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stellenbosch "Stellenbosch"), [Franschhoek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franschhoek "Franschhoek"), [Paarl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paarl "Paarl") and [Barrydale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barrydale "Barrydale").<sup id="cite_ref-320"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup>

### Sports

[![Aerial view of the Cape Town Stadium in Cape Town, South Africa](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/South_Africa_-_Cape_Town_Drieankerbaai_from_Lion%27s_head.jpg/220px-South_Africa_-_Cape_Town_Drieankerbaai_from_Lion%27s_head.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:South_Africa_-_Cape_Town_Drieankerbaai_from_Lion%27s_head.jpg)

[Cape Town Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Town_Stadium "Cape Town Stadium") is the 5th-largest stadium in South Africa, with a capacity of 55,000

South Africa's most popular sports are [association football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_football "Association football"), [rugby union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rugby_union "Rugby union") and [cricket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cricket "Cricket").<sup id="cite_ref-321"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> Other sports with significant support are swimming, athletics, golf, boxing, tennis, [rugby league](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rugby_league "Rugby league"), [ringball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ringball "Ringball"), [field hockey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_hockey "Field hockey"), surfing and [netball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netball "Netball"). Although football (soccer) commands the greatest following among the youth, other sports like basketball, judo, softball and skateboarding are becoming increasingly popular amongst the populace.<sup id="cite_ref-322"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup>

Association football is the most popular sport in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-323"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> Footballers who have played for major foreign clubs include [Steven Pienaar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_Pienaar "Steven Pienaar"), [Lucas Radebe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucas_Radebe "Lucas Radebe"), [Philemon Masinga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philemon_Masinga "Philemon Masinga"), [Benni McCarthy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benni_McCarthy "Benni McCarthy"), [Aaron Mokoena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aaron_Mokoena "Aaron Mokoena"), and [Delron Buckley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delron_Buckley "Delron Buckley"). South Africa hosted the [2010 FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup "2010 FIFA World Cup"), and FIFA president [Sepp Blatter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sepp_Blatter "Sepp Blatter") awarded South Africa a grade 9 out of 10 for successfully hosting the event.<sup id="cite_ref-326"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> Player Benni McCarthy is also a first-team coach for the English football club [Manchester United](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C. "Manchester United F.C.").<sup id="cite_ref-327"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup> It hosted the [1996 African Cup of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1996_African_Cup_of_Nations "1996 African Cup of Nations"), with the national team [Bafana Bafana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa_national_soccer_team "South Africa national soccer team") going on to win the tournament. In 2022, the [women's team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa_women%27s_national_soccer_team "South Africa women's national soccer team") also won the [Women's Africa Cup of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Women%27s_Africa_Cup_of_Nations "2022 Women's Africa Cup of Nations"), beating [Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco_women%27s_national_football_team "Morocco women's national football team") 2–1 in [the final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Women%27s_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_Final "2022 Women's Africa Cup of Nations Final"). The women's team went on to reach the last 16 at the [2023 FIFA Women's World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup "2023 FIFA Women's World Cup"), beating [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy_women%27s_national_football_team "Italy women's national football team") and tying with [Argentina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argentina_women%27s_national_football_team "Argentina women's national football team") in the group stage.

Famous [combat sport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combat_sport "Combat sport") personalities include Baby Jake [Jacob Matlala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_Matlala "Jacob Matlala"), [Vuyani Bungu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vuyani_Bungu "Vuyani Bungu"), [Welcome Ncita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welcome_Ncita "Welcome Ncita"), [Dingaan Thobela](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dingaan_Thobela "Dingaan Thobela"), [Corrie Sanders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corrie_Sanders "Corrie Sanders"), [Gerrie Coetzee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerrie_Coetzee "Gerrie Coetzee"), [Brian Mitchell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Mitchell_(boxer) "Brian Mitchell (boxer)") and [Dricus du Plessis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dricus_du_Plessis "Dricus du Plessis"). Durban surfer [Jordy Smith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordy_Smith "Jordy Smith") won the 2010 Billabong J-Bay Open making him the highest ranked surfer in the world. South Africa produced [Formula One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formula_One "Formula One") motor racing's 1979 world champion [Jody Scheckter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jody_Scheckter "Jody Scheckter"). Famous active [Grand Prix motorcycle racing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Prix_motorcycle_racing "Grand Prix motorcycle racing") personalities include [Brad Binder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brad_Binder "Brad Binder") and his younger brother [Darryn Binder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darryn_Binder "Darryn Binder"). Well-known active cricket players include [Kagiso Rabada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kagiso_Rabada "Kagiso Rabada"), [David Miller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Miller_(South_African_cricketer) "David Miller (South African cricketer)"), [Keshav Maharaj](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keshav_Maharaj "Keshav Maharaj"), [Quinton de Kock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quinton_de_Kock "Quinton de Kock"), [Rilee Rossouw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rilee_Rossouw "Rilee Rossouw"), [Anrich Nortje](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anrich_Nortje "Anrich Nortje"), [Reeza Hendricks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reeza_Hendricks "Reeza Hendricks") and [Faf du Plessis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faf_du_Plessis "Faf du Plessis"); most also participate in the [Indian Premier League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Premier_League "Indian Premier League").

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Bokke_Webb_Ellis-beker_toer_JHB_20191107_145608.jpg/220px-Bokke_Webb_Ellis-beker_toer_JHB_20191107_145608.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bokke_Webb_Ellis-beker_toer_JHB_20191107_145608.jpg)

The [Springboks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa_national_rugby_union_team "South Africa national rugby union team") on their tour of the country after winning the [2019 Rugby World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Rugby_World_Cup "2019 Rugby World Cup")

South Africa has produced numerous world class rugby players, including [Francois Pienaar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francois_Pienaar "Francois Pienaar"), [Joost van der Westhuizen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joost_van_der_Westhuizen "Joost van der Westhuizen"), [Danie Craven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danie_Craven "Danie Craven"), [Os du Randt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Os_du_Randt "Os du Randt"), [Frik du Preez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frik_du_Preez "Frik du Preez"), [Naas Botha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naas_Botha "Naas Botha"), [Frans Steyn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frans_Steyn "Frans Steyn"), [Victor Matfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victor_Matfield "Victor Matfield"), [Bryan Habana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bryan_Habana "Bryan Habana"), [Tendai Mtawarira](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tendai_Mtawarira "Tendai Mtawarira"), [Eben Etzebeth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eben_Etzebeth "Eben Etzebeth"), [Cheslin Kolbe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheslin_Kolbe "Cheslin Kolbe") and [Siya Kolisi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siya_Kolisi "Siya Kolisi"). South Africa has won the [Rugby World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rugby_World_Cup "Rugby World Cup") four times, the most wins of any country. South Africa first won the [1995 Rugby World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1995_Rugby_World_Cup "1995 Rugby World Cup"), which it hosted. They went on to win the tournament again in 2007, 2019 and 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-328"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup>

Cricket is one of the most played sports in South Africa. It has hosted the [2003 Cricket World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_Cricket_World_Cup "2003 Cricket World Cup"), the [2007 World Twenty20 Championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICC_World_Twenty20 "ICC World Twenty20"). South Africa's national cricket team, the [Proteas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa_national_cricket_team "South Africa national cricket team"), have also won the inaugural edition of the [1998 ICC KnockOut Trophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_ICC_KnockOut_Trophy "1998 ICC KnockOut Trophy") by defeating [West Indies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Indies_national_cricket_team "West Indies national cricket team") in the final. The [2023 ICC Women's T20 World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_ICC_Women%27s_T20_World_Cup "2023 ICC Women's T20 World Cup") was hosted in South Africa and the [women's team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa_women%27s_national_cricket_team "South Africa women's national cricket team") came in second place. [South Africa's national blind cricket team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa_national_blind_cricket_team "South Africa national blind cricket team") also went on to win the inaugural edition of the [Blind Cricket World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blind_Cricket_World_Cup "Blind Cricket World Cup") in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-329"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup>

In 2004, the swimming team of [Roland Schoeman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roland_Schoeman "Roland Schoeman"), [Lyndon Ferns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyndon_Ferns "Lyndon Ferns"), [Darian Townsend](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darian_Townsend "Darian Townsend") and [Ryk Neethling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryk_Neethling "Ryk Neethling") won the gold medal at the [Olympic Games in Athens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics "2004 Summer Olympics"), simultaneously breaking the world record in the 4×100 [Freestyle Relay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freestyle_Relay "Freestyle Relay"). [Penny Heyns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penny_Heyns "Penny Heyns") won Olympic Gold in the 1996 [Atlanta Olympic Games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Olympic_Games "Atlanta Olympic Games"), and more recently, swimmers [Tatjana Schoenmaker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatjana_Schoenmaker "Tatjana Schoenmaker") and [Lara van Niekerk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lara_van_Niekerk "Lara van Niekerk") have both broken world records and won gold medals at the Olympic and [Commonwealth Games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonwealth_Games "Commonwealth Games"). In 2012, [Oscar Pistorius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oscar_Pistorius "Oscar Pistorius") became the first double amputee sprinter to compete at the [Olympic Games in London](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics "2012 Summer Olympics"). [Gary Player](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gary_Player "Gary Player") is regarded as one of the greatest golfers of all time, having won the [Career Grand Slam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Slam_(golf) "Grand Slam (golf)"), one of five to have done so.<sup id="cite_ref-330"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup>

157.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa#cite_ref-157 "Jump up")** Lehohla, Pali (5 May 2005). ["Debate over race and censuses not peculiar to SA"](https://web.archive.org/web/20070814143522/http://www.statssa.gov.za/news_archive/05may2005_1.asp). _Business Report_. Archived from [the original](http://www.statssa.gov.za/news_archive/05may2005_1.asp) on 14 August 2007. Retrieved 25 August 2013. Others pointed out that the repeal of the Population Registration Act in 1991 removed any legal basis for specifying 'race'. The Identification Act of 1997 makes no mention of race. On the other hand, the Employment Equity Act speaks of 'designated groups' being 'black people, women and people with disabilities'. The Act defines 'black' as referring to 'Africans, coloureds and Indians'. Apartheid and the racial identification which underpinned it explicitly linked race with differential access to resources and power. If the post-apartheid order was committed to remedying this, race would have to be included in surveys and censuses, so that progress in eradicating the consequences of apartheid could be measured and monitored. This was the reasoning that led to a 'self-identifying' question about 'race' or 'population group' in both the 1996 and 2001 population censuses, and in Statistics SA's household survey programme.

## Further reading

-   _A History of South Africa, Third Edition_. Leonard Thompson. [Yale University Press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yale_University_Press "Yale University Press"). 2001. 384 pages. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [0-300-08776-4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-300-08776-4 "Special:BookSources/0-300-08776-4").

-   _Emerging Johannesburg: Perspectives on the Postapartheid City_. Richard Tomlinson, et al. 2003. 336 pages. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [0-415-93559-8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-415-93559-8 "Special:BookSources/0-415-93559-8")
-   _Making of Modern South Africa: Conquest, Segregation and Apartheid_. Nigel Worden. 2000. 194 pages. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [0-631-21661-8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-631-21661-8 "Special:BookSources/0-631-21661-8").
-   _South Africa: A Narrative History_. [Frank Welsh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Welsh_(writer) "Frank Welsh (writer)"). Kodansha America. 1999. 606 pages. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [1-56836-258-7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-56836-258-7 "Special:BookSources/1-56836-258-7")
-   _South Africa in Contemporary Times_. [Godfrey Mwakikagile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Godfrey_Mwakikagile "Godfrey Mwakikagile"). New Africa Press. 2008. 260 pages. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-0-9802587-3-8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-9802587-3-8 "Special:BookSources/978-0-9802587-3-8").
-   _The Atlas of Changing South Africa_. A. J. Christopher. 2000. 216 pages. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [0-415-21178-6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-415-21178-6 "Special:BookSources/0-415-21178-6").
-   _The Politics of the New South Africa_. Heather Deegan. 2000. 256 pages. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [0-582-38227-0](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-582-38227-0 "Special:BookSources/0-582-38227-0").
